# 9 OpenClaw Projects to Build in 2026: From Reddit Bots to Self-Healing Servers

Build 9 OpenClaw projects, from Reddit digest bots to self-healing servers. Each project includes configs, prompts, and setup guides from the community.

List Contents

Feb 15, 2026  · 10 min read

Contents

* [OpenClaw Projects: Prerequisites](#openclaw-projects:-prerequisites-<span)

* [1. Daily Reddit Digest](#1.-daily-reddit-digest-<span)

* [2. Personal Knowledge Base with RAG](#2.-personal-knowledge-base-with-rag-<imgl)

* [3. Health and Symptom Tracker](#3.-health-and-symptom-tracker-<imgl)

* [4. Overnight Mini-App Builder](#4.-overnight-mini-app-builder-<imgl)

* [5. Personal CRM with Automatic Contact Discovery](#5.-personal-crm-with-automatic-contact-discovery-<imgl)

* [6. Family Calendar and Household Assistant](#6.-family-calendar-and-household-assistant-<span)

* [7. Dynamic Dashboard with Parallel Sub-Agents](#7.-dynamic-dashboard-with-parallel-sub-agents-<imgl)

* [8. Self-Healing Home Server](#8.-self-healing-home-server-<imgl)

* [9. Multi-Agent Specialized Team](#9.-multi-agent-specialized-team-<imgl)

* [Wrap-Up](#wrap-up-<span)

* [OpenClaw Projects FAQs](#faq)

## GroupTraining more people?

Get your team access to the full DataCamp for business platform.[For Business](/business)For a bespoke solution [book a demo](/business/demo-2).

OpenClaw started as a side project to connect LLMs to messaging apps and somehow ended up with 188K GitHub stars. It runs on your hardware, talks to Telegram, Discord, or Slack, and does whatever you configure it to do through tools and prompts. The community around it has gotten creative.

We went through the most popular OpenClaw projects and picked 9 that are actually worth your time. They range from a Reddit digest bot you can wire up in an afternoon to a multi-agent team running on a VPS, and each one comes with documented configs and prompts, so you're not guessing at implementation details.

The list assumes you already have OpenClaw running. If not, our [OpenClaw tutorial](https://www.datacamp.com/tutorial/openclaw-tutorial) covers the setup. 

## OpenClaw Projects: Prerequisites

OpenClaw binds to `0.0.0.0` by default, meaning your instance listens on every network interface the moment you start it. A [Bitdefender audit](https://www.bitdefender.com/en-us/blog/hotforsecurity/135k-openclaw-ai-agents-exposed-online) found over 135,000 instances sitting wide open on the internet because nobody changed that default. A good chunk of those were vulnerable to remote code execution. Change the bind address to `127.0.0.1` in your config before doing anything else.

ClawHub skills deserve the same skepticism as random npm packages. That same audit flagged around 17% of listed skills as malicious, with some designed to steal credentials from your machine. Read the source code before installing anything.

One more thing on setup: Ollama gives you a local LLM (Qwen3 8B, Llama 3.2, whatever fits your RAM) at zero API cost. Good enough for prototyping any project on this list, and you can swap in a cloud model later if you need the horsepower. Our [OpenClaw with Ollama tutorial](https://www.datacamp.com/tutorial/openclaw-ollama-tutorial) walks through the full setup.

## 1. Daily Reddit Digest

![Title: OpenClaw daily Reddit digest workflow showing cron trigger, Reddit API fetch, preference memory, and Telegram delivery - Description: OpenClaw daily Reddit digest workflow showing cron trigger, Reddit API fetch, preference memory, and Telegram delivery](https://media.datacamp.com/cms/f3224755a742257dd5d6e6d2b90fa6ec.png)

You wake up to a Telegram message with the best posts from your favorite subreddits, already filtered to the stuff you actually care about.

It runs on the [reddit-readonly](https://clawhub.ai/buksan1950/reddit-readonly) skill, which pulls hot, new, and top posts plus comment threads without needing Reddit API auth. A cron job triggers the agent on your schedule and it delivers the digest to Telegram. Install the skill, paste in your subreddit list, set the cron time, done. Fifteen minutes, tops. The [full guide](https://github.com/hesamsheikh/awesome-openclaw-usecases/blob/main/usecases/daily-reddit-digest.md) has the exact prompt.

What makes this worth running long-term is the feedback loop. The prompt tells the agent to keep a separate memory file tracking your preferences and to ask daily whether the list hit the mark. A few weeks in, it's filtering out memes on its own, favoring longer discussion posts, skipping reposts. The digest sharpens as the memory file grows.

## 2. Personal Knowledge Base with RAG

![Title: OpenClaw knowledge base pipeline showing URL ingestion, chunking, vector index storage, and semantic retrieval via Telegram - Description: OpenClaw knowledge base pipeline showing URL ingestion, chunking, vector index storage, and semantic retrieval via Telegram](https://media.datacamp.com/cms/17093a9beee602e599b93a7d702a7229.png)

Send a URL to a Telegram chat, and the agent fetches it, chunks the content, and drops it into a searchable index. Articles, tweet threads, YouTube transcripts, and PDFs all go into the same pile.

Later, you ask, "What did I save about vector databases last month?" and get ranked results with sources and excerpts instead of a list of links you bookmarked and forgot. The `knowledge-base` skill handles ingestion and retrieval, while `web_fetch` grabs the raw content. Each time you send a link, the agent confirms what it stored: title, type, and chunk count.

The real payoff comes from stacking this with other workflows. The agent pulls from your knowledge base during meeting prep or content research without being asked, as long as the prompt tells it to query the KB when context fits. You need:

* A Telegram topic or Slack channel for ingestion
* The `knowledge-base` and `web_fetch` skills
* A prompt config covering tagging, confirmation messages, and search behavior

Full prompt is in the [setup guide](https://github.com/hesamsheikh/awesome-openclaw-usecases/blob/main/usecases/knowledge-base-rag.md).

## 3. Health and Symptom Tracker

![Title: OpenClaw health tracker showing daily logging via Telegram reminders, markdown file storage, and weekly pattern analysis - Description: OpenClaw health tracker showing daily logging via Telegram reminders, markdown file storage, and weekly pattern analysis](https://media.datacamp.com/cms/35b60703d8da8a38edccd937561138d6.png)

Message a Telegram topic with what you ate or how you're feeling, and the agent appends a timestamped entry to a markdown file at `~/clawd/memory/health-log.md`. Reminders at 8 AM, 1 PM, and 7 PM keep the data flowing without relying on your memory.

Every Sunday, the agent runs pattern analysis on the week's log and posts back to the same topic: which foods showed up on bad days, whether symptoms cluster around certain meals, and anything that repeats enough to notice. Dairy plus headaches three Wednesdays in a row is the kind of thing it catches.

No skills needed. A prompt and a cron job cover everything, and the [config](https://github.com/hesamsheikh/awesome-openclaw-usecases/blob/main/usecases/health-symptom-tracker.md) is ready to copy. This is the lowest-effort project on the list, which makes it a good starting point if you've never configured an OpenClaw cron job before.

## 4. Overnight Mini-App Builder

![Title: OpenClaw overnight builder workflow showing goal brain dump, daily cron trigger, autonomous session spawning, and morning Telegram summary - Description: OpenClaw overnight builder workflow showing goal brain dump, daily cron trigger, autonomous session spawning, and morning Telegram summary](https://media.datacamp.com/cms/5724f51b418547b7f72df4f0a866a2d7.png)

Tell the agent what you're working toward (a YouTube channel, a SaaS launch, a freelance business) and let it figure out what to build while you sleep. By morning, there's a working mini-app in your project folder and a message in Telegram explaining what it made and why.

The setup is a single long prompt where you dump your goals, interests, and current projects. The agent uses that context to generate 4-5 daily tasks at 8 AM, and one of those tasks is always a small build: a landing page, an automation script, a calculator for something you mentioned needing. 

It spawns a session, writes the code, and moves on to the next task. The `sessions_spawn` and `sessions_send` skills handle the autonomous execution.

What keeps this from being a gimmick is the goal context. The agent connects dots across your brain dump that you might not connect yourself. Mention both "growing a newsletter" and "building analytics tools" and it might prototype a subscriber dashboard you hadn't thought to build. Alex Finn documented the approach in the [original guide](https://github.com/hesamsheikh/awesome-openclaw-usecases/blob/main/usecases/overnight-mini-app-builder.md).

## 5. Personal CRM with Automatic Contact Discovery

![Title: OpenClaw personal CRM showing dual cron jobs scanning Gmail and Google Calendar, SQLite storage, and natural language Telegram queries - Description: OpenClaw personal CRM showing dual cron jobs scanning Gmail and Google Calendar, SQLite storage, and natural language Telegram queries](https://media.datacamp.com/cms/6c64bfaf82ee91849fc664c1f6decfc4.png)

A cron job at 6 AM scans your Gmail and Google Calendar for anyone you interacted with in the last 24 hours. New contacts go into a SQLite database. Existing ones get their interaction count bumped and notes updated. By the time you're awake, yesterday's meetings and emails are already logged.

A second cron at 7 AM checks your calendar for the day ahead and builds a briefing on each external attendee: when you last talked, what you discussed, and anything that needs follow-up. That briefing lands in a dedicated Telegram topic before your first meeting starts.

Between the scheduled jobs, you can query the CRM in natural language through the same Telegram topic. "Who needs follow-up?" and "What do I know about Sarah?" both work. The setup needs:

* The `gog` CLI for Gmail and Google Calendar access
* A SQLite database with a contacts table (the [guide](https://github.com/hesamsheikh/awesome-openclaw-usecases/blob/main/usecases/personal-crm.md) has the schema)
* Two cron jobs and a Telegram topic

## 6. Family Calendar and Household Assistant

Calendar fragmentation is the problem here. Work calendars with restricted sharing, school schedules buried in PDFs, camp dates in email threads, appointment confirmations in text messages. This project pulls all of it into a single morning briefing at 8 AM with a 3-day conflict lookahead and weather context.

The more interesting piece is ambient iMessage monitoring. Every 15 minutes, the agent scans for patterns like "your appointment is confirmed for Tuesday at 2 PM" and auto-creates a calendar event with 30-minute driving buffers on both sides. It catches promises, too. "I'll send that over by Friday" becomes a calendar hold so you don't forget.

Pantry tracking rounds it out. Snap a photo of your fridge or a receipt, and the vision model extracts items into an inventory file. Ask "Do we have butter?" through Telegram, and you get back a location and quantity. "Generate grocery list" compiles everything that's running low.

This one runs best on a Mac Mini since it needs iMessage access and always-on availability. Start with calendar reading only and add write actions (event creation, inventory updates) once you trust the agent's judgment. The full [setup walkthrough](https://github.com/hesamsheikh/awesome-openclaw-usecases/blob/main/usecases/family-calendar-household-assistant.md) covers the phased rollout.

## 7. Dynamic Dashboard with Parallel Sub-Agents

![Title: OpenClaw dynamic dashboard architecture showing parallel sub-agents fetching from GitHub, Twitter, and system metrics, with PostgreSQL storage and Discord alerts - Description: OpenClaw dynamic dashboard architecture showing parallel sub-agents fetching from GitHub, Twitter, and system metrics, with PostgreSQL storage and Discord alerts](https://media.datacamp.com/cms/9d2240b5621280682a6daea6d5bc99d2.png)

Every 15 minutes, a cron job spawns sub-agents that fan out to GitHub, Twitter, your server metrics, and whatever other APIs you care about. Each one fetches its data and reports back. The main agent collects everything, formats it into a Discord message, and posts to a `#dashboard` channel.

Fetching sequentially would be the obvious approach, but API latency stacks up fast when Twitter rate-limits you and SSH health checks take their time. Sub-agents run in parallel so a slow source doesn't block the rest.

A PostgreSQL `metrics` table stores every data point with timestamps. "How did GitHub stars move this week?" works because the history is queryable, not because the agent remembers. Alert conditions sit in a separate table: star count spikes over 50 in an hour, CPU above 90%, and negative sentiment clusters on Twitter. When a threshold trips, the Discord message gets an alert flag instead of waiting for the next scheduled cycle. SQL schema and cron config are in the [setup guide](https://github.com/hesamsheikh/awesome-openclaw-usecases/blob/main/usecases/dynamic-dashboard.md).

## 8. Self-Healing Home Server

![Title: OpenClaw self-healing server showing Reef agent's cron schedule, kubectl remediation loop, and security pipeline with TruffleHog and Gitea - Description: OpenClaw self-healing server showing Reef agent's cron schedule, kubectl remediation loop, and security pipeline with TruffleHog and Gitea](https://media.datacamp.com/cms/08f84b378b89cfa2e131690f5de898b9.png)

Nathan runs an agent called Reef on a home Kubernetes cluster, and it operates as a junior sysadmin that never sleeps. Reef has SSH access to every machine on the local network, credentials in a dedicated 1Password vault, and enough tooling (Terraform, Ansible, kubectl) to fix problems without waking anyone up.

The cron schedule is dense. Health checks against Gatus and ArgoCD run hourly, kanban board scans every 15 minutes, and a 6-hour rotation audits disk usage, memory, and Loki logs. The 8 AM briefing pulls weather, both partners' calendars, system health across all machines, service status, recent ArgoCD deployments, task board progress, and email action items into a single Telegram message.

Reef doesn't just alert on a failing pod. It runs `kubectl` to restart it, confirms the fix held, and only pings Nathan when the problem persists after intervention. That closed loop is the difference between a monitoring stack and an agent with agency.

The security setup reflects a hard lesson from day one, when the agent hardcoded an API key into a commit and pushed it. Now TruffleHog pre-push hooks block secrets, changes go through a private Gitea instance before reaching GitHub, and branch protection forces PRs to main. Nathan's [full writeup](https://github.com/hesamsheikh/awesome-openclaw-usecases/blob/main/usecases/self-healing-home-server.md) covers every cron job and the phased rollout.

## 9. Multi-Agent Specialized Team

![Title: OpenClaw multi-agent team with four agents around a Telegram group hub, shared memory files, and per-agent private context folders - Description: OpenClaw multi-agent team with four agents around a Telegram group hub, shared memory files, and per-agent private context folders](https://media.datacamp.com/cms/544d12b091a0d714891168802657b55e.png)

A single Telegram group, four agents, each running a different model. Milo is the strategy lead on Claude Opus and owns the 8 AM standup review. Josh pulls business metrics on Sonnet at 9. 

A marketing agent generates content ideas on Gemini by 10. The dev agent watches CI/CD and reviews PRs throughout the day, and Milo closes things out with a 6 PM recap. Tag `@milo`, `@josh`, `@dev`, or `@all` to route messages. Untagged messages default to Milo.

Shared memory lives on disk. `GOALS.md` holds OKRs, `DECISIONS.md` is append-only so no agent overwrites another's conclusions, and `PROJECT_STATUS.md` tracks shared state. Each agent also gets a private folder for the domain context that the others don't touch.

Two things worth knowing from people who've run this. Personality in the system prompt affects output quality more than model size for most tasks. And matching models to workload saves real money: Gemini handles trend monitoring fine, while Opus earns its cost on strategy reasoning where depth matters.

Start with two agents and add others once you see where coordination breaks down. The [routing config and prompt templates](https://github.com/hesamsheikh/awesome-openclaw-usecases/blob/main/usecases/multi-agent-team.md) are ready to copy.

## Wrap-Up

Every OpenClaw project on this list came from someone who set up OpenClaw, got curious, and pushed it further than the defaults. The Reddit digest and health tracker take an afternoon. A weekend covers the CRM or family calendar if you're comfortable with cron scheduling. The self-healing server and multi-agent team are longer commitments that grow alongside your infrastructure.

Our [introductory tutorial](https://www.datacamp.com/tutorial/openclaw-tutorial) and [Ollama integration guide](https://www.datacamp.com/tutorial/openclaw-ollama-tutorial) cover the foundation if you're starting fresh.

Pick one, get it running, and let the community on GitHub and Discord fill in the gaps when you hit something the guide doesn't cover.

## OpenClaw Projects FAQs

### Do I need a paid API key to build these OpenClaw projects?

**No. You can prototype every project on this list using Ollama with a local model like Qwen3 8B at zero cost. Switch to a cloud API like OpenAI or Anthropic later if you need stronger reasoning or faster responses.**

### Which messaging app works best with OpenClaw?

**Telegram is the most common choice in these projects because of its bot API and topic-based chat organization. Discord and Slack also work, and several projects (like the dynamic dashboard) use Discord instead.**

### How long does it take to set up one of these projects?

**The simpler ones (Reddit digest, health tracker) take under an hour if OpenClaw is already running. Mid-range projects like the personal CRM need a weekend. The self-healing server and multi-agent team are ongoing builds that grow over weeks.**

### Is it safe to give OpenClaw SSH access to my servers?

**It can be, with precautions. The self-healing server project covers this in detail: use a dedicated 1Password vault with limited scope, TruffleHog pre-push hooks to block leaked secrets, branch protection, and a private Gitea instance as a staging layer before GitHub.**

### Can I run multiple OpenClaw agents on the same machine?

Yes. The multi-agent team project runs four agents on a single VPS, each with its own model, personality, and scheduled tasks. Bind each instance to a different port and route messages through Telegram tags.

Each project includes configs, prompts, and setup guides from the community.","type":"article","readTime":"10","isCodeExecutable":false,"authors":[{"id":473,"fullName":"Bex Tuychiev","profileSlug":"bexgboost","shortBio":"Bex is a Top 10 AI writer on Medium and a Kaggle Master with over 15k followers. It runs on your hardware, talks to Telegram, Discord, or Slack, and does whatever you configure it to do through tools and prompts. The community around it has gotten creative.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eWe went through the most popular OpenClaw projects and picked 9 that are actually worth your time. They range from a Reddit digest bot you can wire up in an afternoon to a multi-agent team running on a VPS, and each one comes with documented configs and prompts, so you're not guessing at implementation details.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eThe list assumes you already have OpenClaw running. If not, our\u003c/span\u003e\u003ca style=\"text-decoration: none;\" href=\"https://www.datacamp.com/tutorial/openclaw-tutorial\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e \u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: underline; -webkit-text-decoration-skip: none; text-decoration-skip-ink: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eOpenClaw tutorial\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e covers the setup.\u0026nbsp;\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 dir=\"ltr\"\u003eOpenClaw Projects: Prerequisites\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eOpenClaw binds to \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode\u003e0.0.0.0\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e by default, meaning your instance listens on every network interface the moment you start it. A\u003c/span\u003e\u003ca style=\"text-decoration: none;\" href=\"https://www.bitdefender.com/en-us/blog/hotforsecurity/135k-openclaw-ai-agents-exposed-online\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e \u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: underline; -webkit-text-decoration-skip: none; text-decoration-skip-ink: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eBitdefender audit\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e found over 135,000 instances sitting wide open on the internet because nobody changed that default. A good chunk of those were vulnerable to remote code execution. Change the bind address to \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode\u003e127.0.0.1\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e in your config before doing anything else.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eClawHub skills deserve the same skepticism as random npm packages. That same audit flagged around 17% of listed skills as malicious, with some designed to steal credentials from your machine. Read the source code before installing anything.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eOne more thing on setup: Ollama gives you a local LLM (Qwen3 8B, Llama 3.2, whatever fits your RAM) at zero API cost. Good enough for prototyping any project on this list, and you can swap in a cloud model later if you need the horsepower. Our\u003c/span\u003e\u003ca style=\"text-decoration: none;\" href=\"https://www.datacamp.com/tutorial/openclaw-ollama-tutorial\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e \u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: underline; -webkit-text-decoration-skip: none; text-decoration-skip-ink: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eOpenClaw with Ollama tutorial\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e walks through the full setup.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 dir=\"ltr\"\u003e1. Daily Reddit Digest\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\" style=\"text-align: center;\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: bold; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"border: none; display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; width: 432px; height: 240px;\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://media.datacamp.com/cms/f3224755a742257dd5d6e6d2b90fa6ec.png\" alt=\"Title: OpenClaw daily Reddit digest workflow showing cron trigger, Reddit API fetch, preference memory, and Telegram delivery - Description: OpenClaw daily Reddit digest workflow showing cron trigger, Reddit API fetch, preference memory, and Telegram delivery\" width=\"432\" height=\"240\" /\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eYou wake up to a Telegram message with the best posts from your favorite subreddits, already filtered to the stuff you actually care about.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eIt runs on the\u003c/span\u003e\u003ca style=\"text-decoration: none;\" href=\"https://clawhub.ai/buksan1950/reddit-readonly\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e \u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: underline; -webkit-text-decoration-skip: none; text-decoration-skip-ink: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003ereddit-readonly\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e skill, which pulls hot, new, and top posts plus comment threads without needing Reddit API auth. A cron job triggers the agent on your schedule and it delivers the digest to Telegram. Install the skill, paste in your subreddit list, set the cron time, done. Fifteen minutes, tops. The\u003c/span\u003e\u003ca style=\"text-decoration: none;\" href=\"https://github.com/hesamsheikh/awesome-openclaw-usecases/blob/main/usecases/daily-reddit-digest.md\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e \u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: underline; -webkit-text-decoration-skip: none; text-decoration-skip-ink: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003efull guide\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e has the exact prompt.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eWhat makes this worth running long-term is the feedback loop. The prompt tells the agent to keep a separate memory file tracking your preferences and to ask daily whether the list hit the mark. A few weeks in, it's filtering out memes on its own, favoring longer discussion posts, skipping reposts. The digest sharpens as the memory file grows.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 dir=\"ltr\"\u003e2. Personal Knowledge Base with RAG\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cimg style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\" src=\"https://media.datacamp.com/cms/17093a9beee602e599b93a7d702a7229.png\" alt=\"Title: OpenClaw knowledge base pipeline showing URL ingestion, chunking, vector index storage, and semantic retrieval via Telegram - Description: OpenClaw knowledge base pipeline showing URL ingestion, chunking, vector index storage, and semantic retrieval via Telegram\" width=\"432\" height=\"240\" /\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eSend a URL to a Telegram chat, and the agent fetches it, chunks the content, and drops it into a searchable index. Articles, tweet threads, YouTube transcripts, and PDFs all go into the same pile.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eLater, you ask, \"What did I save about vector databases last month?\" and get ranked results with sources and excerpts instead of a list of links you bookmarked and forgot. The \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode\u003eknowledge-base\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e skill handles ingestion and retrieval, while \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode\u003eweb\_fetch\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e grabs the raw content. Each time you send a link, the agent confirms what it stored: title, type, and chunk count.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eThe real payoff comes from stacking this with other workflows. The agent pulls from your knowledge base during meeting prep or content research without being asked, as long as the prompt tells it to query the KB when context fits. You need:\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul style=\"padding-inline-start: 48px;\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eA Telegram topic or Slack channel for ingestion\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eThe \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode\u003eknowledge-base\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e and \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode\u003eweb\_fetch\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e skills\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eA prompt config covering tagging, confirmation messages, and search behavior\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eFull prompt is in the\u003c/span\u003e\u003ca style=\"text-decoration: none;\" href=\"https://github.com/hesamsheikh/awesome-openclaw-usecases/blob/main/usecases/knowledge-base-rag.md\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 dir=\"ltr\"\u003e3. Health and Symptom Tracker\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cimg style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\" src=\"https://media.datacamp.com/cms/35b60703d8da8a38edccd937561138d6.png\" alt=\"Title: OpenClaw health tracker showing daily logging via Telegram reminders, markdown file storage, and weekly pattern analysis - Description: OpenClaw health tracker showing daily logging via Telegram reminders, markdown file storage, and weekly pattern analysis\" width=\"432\" height=\"240\" /\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eMessage a Telegram topic with what you ate or how you're feeling, and the agent appends a timestamped entry to a markdown file at \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode\u003e~/clawd/memory/health-log.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e. Reminders at 8 AM, 1 PM, and 7 PM keep the data flowing without relying on your memory.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eEvery Sunday, the agent runs pattern analysis on the week's log and posts back to the same topic: which foods showed up on bad days, whether symptoms cluster around certain meals, and anything that repeats enough to notice. Dairy plus headaches three Wednesdays in a row is the kind of thing it catches.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eNo skills needed. A prompt and a cron job cover everything, and the\u003c/span\u003e\u003ca style=\"text-decoration: none;\" href=\"https://github.com/hesamsheikh/awesome-openclaw-usecases/blob/main/usecases/health-symptom-tracker.md\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e \u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: underline; -webkit-text-decoration-skip: none; text-decoration-skip-ink: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003econfig\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e is ready to copy. This is the lowest-effort project on the list, which makes it a good starting point if you've never configured an OpenClaw cron job before.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 dir=\"ltr\"\u003e4. Overnight Mini-App Builder\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cimg style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\" src=\"https://media.datacamp.com/cms/5724f51b418547b7f72df4f0a866a2d7.png\" alt=\"Title: OpenClaw overnight builder workflow showing goal brain dump, daily cron trigger, autonomous session spawning, and morning Telegram summary - Description: OpenClaw overnight builder workflow showing goal brain dump, daily cron trigger, autonomous session spawning, and morning Telegram summary\" width=\"432\" height=\"240\" /\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eTell the agent what you're working toward (a YouTube channel, a SaaS launch, a freelance business) and let it figure out what to build while you sleep. By morning, there's a working mini-app in your project folder and a message in Telegram explaining what it made and why.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eThe setup is a single long prompt where you dump your goals, interests, and current projects. The agent uses that context to generate 4-5 daily tasks at 8 AM, and one of those tasks is always a small build: a landing page, an automation script, a calculator for something you mentioned needing.\u0026nbsp;\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eIt spawns a session, writes the code, and moves on to the next task. The \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode\u003esessions\_spawn\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e and \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode\u003esessions\_send\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e skills handle the autonomous execution.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eWhat keeps this from being a gimmick is the goal context. The agent connects dots across your brain dump that you might not connect yourself. Mention both \"growing a newsletter\" and \"building analytics tools\" and it might prototype a subscriber dashboard you hadn't thought to build. Alex Finn documented the approach in the\u003c/span\u003e\u003ca style=\"text-decoration: none;\" href=\"https://github.com/hesamsheikh/awesome-openclaw-usecases/blob/main/usecases/overnight-mini-app-builder.md\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e \u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: underline; -webkit-text-decoration-skip: none; text-decoration-skip-ink: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eoriginal guide\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 dir=\"ltr\"\u003e5. Personal CRM with Automatic Contact Discovery\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cimg style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\" src=\"https://media.datacamp.com/cms/6c64bfaf82ee91849fc664c1f6decfc4.png\" alt=\"Title: OpenClaw personal CRM showing dual cron jobs scanning Gmail and Google Calendar, SQLite storage, and natural language Telegram queries - Description: OpenClaw personal CRM showing dual cron jobs scanning Gmail and Google Calendar, SQLite storage, and natural language Telegram queries\" width=\"432\" height=\"240\" /\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eA cron job at 6 AM scans your Gmail and Google Calendar for anyone you interacted with in the last 24 hours. New contacts go into a SQLite database. Existing ones get their interaction count bumped and notes updated. By the time you're awake, yesterday's meetings and emails are already logged.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eA second cron at 7 AM checks your calendar for the day ahead and builds a briefing on each external attendee: when you last talked, what you discussed, and anything that needs follow-up. That briefing lands in a dedicated Telegram topic before your first meeting starts.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eBetween the scheduled jobs, you can query the CRM in natural language through the same Telegram topic. \"Who needs follow-up?\" and \"What do I know about Sarah?\" both work. The setup needs:\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul style=\"padding-inline-start: 48px;\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eThe \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode\u003egog\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e CLI for Gmail and Google Calendar access\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eA SQLite database with a contacts table (the\u003c/span\u003e\u003ca style=\"text-decoration: none;\" href=\"https://github.com/hesamsheikh/awesome-openclaw-usecases/blob/main/usecases/personal-crm.md\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e \u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: underline; -webkit-text-decoration-skip: none; text-decoration-skip-ink: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eguide\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e has the schema)\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eTwo cron jobs and a Telegram topic\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003ch2 dir=\"ltr\"\u003e6. Family Calendar and Household Assistant\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eCalendar fragmentation is the problem here. Work calendars with restricted sharing, school schedules buried in PDFs, camp dates in email threads, appointment confirmations in text messages. This project pulls all of it into a single morning briefing at 8 AM with a 3-day conflict lookahead and weather context.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eThe more interesting piece is ambient iMessage monitoring. Every 15 minutes, the agent scans for patterns like \"your appointment is confirmed for Tuesday at 2 PM\" and auto-creates a calendar event with 30-minute driving buffers on both sides. It catches promises, too. \"I'll send that over by Friday\" becomes a calendar hold so you don't forget.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003ePantry tracking rounds it out. Snap a photo of your fridge or a receipt, and the vision model extracts items into an inventory file. Ask \"Do we have butter?\" through Telegram, and you get back a location and quantity. \"Generate grocery list\" compiles everything that's running low.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eThis one runs best on a Mac Mini since it needs iMessage access and always-on availability. Start with calendar reading only and add write actions (event creation, inventory updates) once you trust the agent's judgment. The full\u003c/span\u003e\u003ca style=\"text-decoration: none;\" href=\"https://github.com/hesamsheikh/awesome-openclaw-usecases/blob/main/usecases/family-calendar-household-assistant.md\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e \u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: underline; -webkit-text-decoration-skip: none; text-decoration-skip-ink: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003esetup walkthrough\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e covers the phased rollout.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 dir=\"ltr\"\u003e7. Dynamic Dashboard with Parallel Sub-Agents\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cimg style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\" src=\"https://media.datacamp.com/cms/9d2240b5621280682a6daea6d5bc99d2.png\" alt=\"Title: OpenClaw dynamic dashboard architecture showing parallel sub-agents fetching from GitHub, Twitter, and system metrics, with PostgreSQL storage and Discord alerts - Description: OpenClaw dynamic dashboard architecture showing parallel sub-agents fetching from GitHub, Twitter, and system metrics, with PostgreSQL storage and Discord alerts\" width=\"432\" height=\"240\" /\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eEvery 15 minutes, a cron job spawns sub-agents that fan out to GitHub, Twitter, your server metrics, and whatever other APIs you care about. Each one fetches its data and reports back. The main agent collects everything, formats it into a Discord message, and posts to a \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode\u003e#dashboard\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e channel.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eFetching sequentially would be the obvious approach, but API latency stacks up fast when Twitter rate-limits you and SSH health checks take their time. Sub-agents run in parallel so a slow source doesn't block the rest.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eA PostgreSQL \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode\u003emetrics\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e table stores every data point with timestamps. \"How did GitHub stars move this week?\" works because the history is queryable, not because the agent remembers. Alert conditions sit in a separate table: star count spikes over 50 in an hour, CPU above 90%, and negative sentiment clusters on Twitter. When a threshold trips, the Discord message gets an alert flag instead of waiting for the next scheduled cycle. SQL schema and cron config are in the\u003c/span\u003e\u003ca style=\"text-decoration: none;\" href=\"https://github.com/hesamsheikh/awesome-openclaw-usecases/blob/main/usecases/dynamic-dashboard.md\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e \u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: underline; -webkit-text-decoration-skip: none; text-decoration-skip-ink: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003esetup guide\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 dir=\"ltr\"\u003e8. Self-Healing Home Server\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cimg style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\" src=\"https://media.datacamp.com/cms/08f84b378b89cfa2e131690f5de898b9.png\" alt=\"Title: OpenClaw self-healing server showing Reef agent's cron schedule, kubectl remediation loop, and security pipeline with TruffleHog and Gitea - Description: OpenClaw self-healing server showing Reef agent's cron schedule, kubectl remediation loop, and security pipeline with TruffleHog and Gitea\" width=\"432\" height=\"240\" /\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eNathan runs an agent called Reef on a home Kubernetes cluster, and it operates as a junior sysadmin that never sleeps. Reef has SSH access to every machine on the local network, credentials in a dedicated 1Password vault, and enough tooling (Terraform, Ansible, kubectl) to fix problems without waking anyone up.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eThe cron schedule is dense. Health checks against Gatus and ArgoCD run hourly, kanban board scans every 15 minutes, and a 6-hour rotation audits disk usage, memory, and Loki logs. The 8 AM briefing pulls weather, both partners' calendars, system health across all machines, service status, recent ArgoCD deployments, task board progress, and email action items into a single Telegram message.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eReef doesn't just alert on a failing pod. It runs \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode\u003ekubectl\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e to restart it, confirms the fix held, and only pings Nathan when the problem persists after intervention. That closed loop is the difference between a monitoring stack and an agent with agency.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eThe security setup reflects a hard lesson from day one, when the agent hardcoded an API key into a commit and pushed it. Now TruffleHog pre-push hooks block secrets, changes go through a private Gitea instance before reaching GitHub, and branch protection forces PRs to main. Nathan's\u003c/span\u003e\u003ca style=\"text-decoration: none;\" href=\"https://github.com/hesamsheikh/awesome-openclaw-usecases/blob/main/usecases/self-healing-home-server.md\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e \u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: underline; -webkit-text-decoration-skip: none; text-decoration-skip-ink: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003efull writeup\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e covers every cron job and the phased rollout.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 dir=\"ltr\"\u003e9. Multi-Agent Specialized Team\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cimg style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\" src=\"https://media.datacamp.com/cms/544d12b091a0d714891168802657b55e.png\" alt=\"Title: OpenClaw multi-agent team with four agents around a Telegram group hub, shared memory files, and per-agent private context folders - Description: OpenClaw multi-agent team with four agents around a Telegram group hub, shared memory files, and per-agent private context folders\" width=\"432\" height=\"240\" /\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eA single Telegram group, four agents, each running a different model. Milo is the strategy lead on Claude Opus and owns the 8 AM standup review. Josh pulls business metrics on Sonnet at 9.\u0026nbsp;\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eA marketing agent generates content ideas on Gemini by 10. The dev agent watches CI/CD and reviews PRs throughout the day, and Milo closes things out with a 6 PM recap. Tag \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode\u003e@milo\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e, \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode\u003e@josh\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e, \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode\u003e@dev\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e, or \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode\u003e@all\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e to route messages. Untagged messages default to Milo.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eShared memory lives on disk. \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode\u003eGOALS.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e holds OKRs, \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode\u003eDECISIONS.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e is append-only so no agent overwrites another's conclusions, and \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode\u003ePROJECT\_STATUS.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e tracks shared state. Each agent also gets a private folder for the domain context that the others don't touch.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eTwo things worth knowing from people who've run this. Personality in the system prompt affects output quality more than model size for most tasks. And matching models to workload saves real money: Gemini handles trend monitoring fine, while Opus earns its cost on strategy reasoning where depth matters.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eStart with two agents and add others once you see where coordination breaks down. The\u003c/span\u003e\u003ca style=\"text-decoration: none;\" href=\"https://github.com/hesamsheikh/awesome-openclaw-usecases/blob/main/usecases/multi-agent-team.md\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e \u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: underline; -webkit-text-decoration-skip: none; text-decoration-skip-ink: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003erouting config and prompt templates\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003e are ready to copy.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 dir=\"ltr\"\u003eWrap-Up\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"ltr\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"background-color: transparent; font-weight: 400; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"\u003eEvery OpenClaw project on this list came from someone who set up OpenClaw, got curious, and pushed it further than the defaults.
